	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Huddersfield</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

<span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Huddersfield&amp;params=53.645_N_1.7798_W_region:GB_type:city(162949)"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">53°38′42″N</span> <span class="longitude">1°46′47″W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">53.6450°N 1.7798°W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">53.6450; -1.7798</span></span></span></a></span><span style="font-size: small;"><span id="coordinates"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Coordinates</a>: <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Huddersfield&amp;params=53.645_N_1.7798_W_region:GB_type:city(162949)"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">53°38′42″N</span> <span class="longitude">1°46′47″W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">53.6450°N 1.7798°W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">53.6450; -1.7798</span></span></span></a></span></span></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Huddersfield</b> is a large <a href="/wiki/Market_town" title="Market town">market</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_town" class="mw-redirect" title="University town">university town</a><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> in West Yorkshire, England. It is the 11th largest town in the United Kingdom, with a population of 162,949 at the 2011 census.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> It lies 14 miles (23&#160;km) southwest of <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a> and 24 miles (39&#160;km) northeast of <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>.
</p><p>Huddersfield is near the confluence of the <a href="/wiki/River_Colne,_West_Yorkshire" title="River Colne, West Yorkshire">River Colne</a> and the <a href="/wiki/River_Holme" title="River Holme">River Holme</a>. Within the <a href="/wiki/Historic_counties_of_England" title="Historic counties of England">historic county boundaries</a> of the <a href="/wiki/West_Riding_of_Yorkshire" title="West Riding of Yorkshire">West Riding of Yorkshire</a>, it is the largest urban area in the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_borough" title="Metropolitan borough">metropolitan borough</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kirklees" title="Kirklees">Kirklees</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Administrative_centre" title="Administrative centre">administrative centre</a> of the borough. The town is known for its role in the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, and for being the birthplaces of <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a>, <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a>, and the film star <a href="/wiki/James_Mason" title="James Mason">James Mason</a>.
</p><p>Huddersfield is home to rugby league team <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Giants" title="Huddersfield Giants">Huddersfield Giants</a>, founded in 1895, who play in the <a href="/wiki/Super_League" title="Super League">Super League</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Championship">Championship</a> <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> team <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Town_A.F.C." title="Huddersfield Town A.F.C.">Huddersfield Town A.F.C.</a>, founded in 1908. The town is home to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Huddersfield" title="University of Huddersfield">University of Huddersfield</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sixth_form" title="Sixth form">sixth form</a> colleges <a href="/wiki/Greenhead_College" title="Greenhead College">Greenhead College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kirklees_College" title="Kirklees College">Kirklees College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_New_College" title="Huddersfield New College">Huddersfield New College</a>.
</p><p>Huddersfield is a town of <a href="/wiki/Victorian_architecture" title="Victorian architecture">Victorian architecture</a>. <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_railway_station" title="Huddersfield railway station">Huddersfield railway station</a> is a Grade I <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">listed building</a> described by <a href="/wiki/John_Betjeman" title="John Betjeman">John Betjeman</a> as "the most splendid station façade in England", second only to <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_railway_station" title="St Pancras railway station">St Pancras, London</a>. The station in St George's Square was renovated at a cost of £4&#160;million<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> and subsequently won the <a href="/wiki/Europa_Nostra" title="Europa Nostra">Europa Nostra</a> award for European architecture.
</p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Landmarks_and_architecture"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Landmarks and architecture</span></a></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There has been a settlement in the area for over 4,000 years.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The remains of a <a href="/wiki/Castra" title="Castra">Roman fort</a> were unearthed in the mid 18th century at <a href="/wiki/Slack_Roman_fort" class="mw-redirect" title="Slack Roman fort">Slack</a> near <a href="/wiki/Outlane" title="Outlane">Outlane</a>, west of the town.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Castle_Hill,_Huddersfield" title="Castle Hill, Huddersfield">Castle Hill</a>, a major landmark, was the site of an <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> <a href="/wiki/Hill_fort" class="mw-redirect" title="Hill fort">hill fort</a>. Huddersfield was recorded in the <i><a href="/wiki/Domesday_Book" title="Domesday Book">Domesday Book</a></i> of 1086 as <i>Oderesfelt</i> and <i>Odresfeld</i>. Indeed, the modern name <i>Huddersfield</i> is pronounced without a word-initial /h/ in the local dialect, suggesting that the <a href="/wiki/Standard_English" title="Standard English">standard English</a> pronunciation has influenced the commonly accepted spelling.
</p><p>Huddersfield has been a <a href="/wiki/Market_town" title="Market town">market town</a> since <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Anglo-Saxon</a> times. The <a href="/wiki/Market_cross" title="Market cross">market cross</a> is on Market Place.
</p><p>The manor of Huddersfield was owned by the <a href="/wiki/De_Lacy_family" class="mw-redirect" title="De Lacy family">de Lacy family</a> until 1322, at which it reverted to royal ownership. In 1599, <a href="/w/index.php?title=William_Ramsden_(died_1623)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="William Ramsden (died 1623) (page does not exist)">William Ramsden</a> bought the manor, and the <a href="/wiki/Ramsden_baronets" title="Ramsden baronets">Ramsden family</a> continued to own the manor, which came to be known as the 'Ramsden Estate', until 1920. During their ownership they supported the development of the town. <a href="/wiki/Sir_John_Ramsden,_3rd_Baronet" title="Sir John Ramsden, 3rd Baronet">Sir John Ramsden, 3rd Baronet</a> built the Huddersfield Cloth Hall in 1766 and the his son <a href="/wiki/Sir_John_Ramsden,_4th_Baronet" title="Sir John Ramsden, 4th Baronet">the fourth baronet</a> was responsible for <a href="/wiki/Sir_John_Ramsden%27s_Canal" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir John Ramsden&#39;s Canal">Sir John Ramsden's Canal</a> in 1780. The Ramsdens also supported the arrival of the railway in the 1840s.<sup id="cite_ref-hudhist_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hudhist-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:602px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Huddersfield1000px(RLH).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Huddersfield1000px%28RLH%29.jpg/600px-Huddersfield1000px%28RLH%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="600" height="230" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Huddersfield1000px%28RLH%29.jpg/900px-Huddersfield1000px%28RLH%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Huddersfield1000px%28RLH%29.jpg/1200px-Huddersfield1000px%28RLH%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2281" data-file-height="874" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Huddersfield1000px(RLH).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Huddersfield, viewed from <a href="/wiki/Castle_Hill,_Huddersfield" title="Castle Hill, Huddersfield">Castle Hill</a></div></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_Revolution">Industrial Revolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Industrial Revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Huddersfield was a centre of civil unrest during the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>. In a period where Europe was experiencing frequent wars, where trade had slumped and the crops had failed, many local <a href="/wiki/Weaver_(occupation)" class="mw-redirect" title="Weaver (occupation)">weavers</a> faced losing their livelihood due to the introduction of machinery in factories. <a href="/wiki/Luddite" title="Luddite">Luddites</a> began destroying mills and machinery in response; one of the most notorious attacks was on Cartwright – a Huddersfield mill-owner, who had a reputation for cruelty – and his Rawfolds Mill. In his book <i>Rebels Against the Future</i>, <a href="/wiki/Kirkpatrick_Sale" title="Kirkpatrick Sale">Kirkpatrick Sale</a> describes how an army platoon was stationed at Huddersfield to deal with Luddites; at its peak, there were about a thousand soldiers in Huddersfield and ten thousand civilians. In response, Luddites began to focus attacks on nearby towns and villages, which were less well-protected; the largest act of damage that they committed was the destruction of Foster's Mill at <a href="/wiki/Horbury" title="Horbury">Horbury</a> – a village about 10 miles (16&#160;km) east of Huddersfield.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The government campaign that crushed the movement was provoked by a murder that took place in Huddersfield. William Horsfall, a mill-owner and a passionate prosecutor of Luddites, was killed in 1812.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Although the movement faded out, Parliament began to increase welfare provision for those out of work, and introduce regulations to improve conditions in the mills.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_history">Political history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Political history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Two Prime Ministers spent part of their childhood in Huddersfield: <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a> and <a href="/wiki/H._H._Asquith" title="H. H. Asquith">H. H. Asquith</a>. Wilson is commemorated by a statue in front of the railway station.
</p><p>The Huddersfield constituency has been represented by Labour MP Barry Sheerman since its creation in 1983 and is considered a safe seat for Labour.
</p><p>Kirklees Council was the first in the UK to have a <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales" title="Green Party of England and Wales">Green Party</a> councillor, Nicholas Harvey who was instrumental in protesting against the intended closure of the <a href="/wiki/Settle_and_Carlisle_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Settle and Carlisle Railway">Settle and Carlisle Railway</a> line.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The town has substantial Labour, <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a>, Liberal Democrats and <a href="/wiki/UKIP" class="mw-redirect" title="UKIP">UKIP</a> presences.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:107px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Huddersfield-coa.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/6/6f/Huddersfield-coa.gif" decoding="async" width="105" height="133" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="105" data-file-height="133" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Huddersfield-coa.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Huddersfield" title="Coat of arms of Huddersfield">Coat of arms of the former County Borough</a></div></div></div>
<p>Huddersfield was incorporated as a <a href="/wiki/Municipal_borough" title="Municipal borough">municipal borough</a> in the ancient <a href="/wiki/West_Riding_of_Yorkshire" title="West Riding of Yorkshire">West Riding of Yorkshire</a> in 1868. The borough comprised the parishes of Almondbury, Dalton, Huddersfield, Lindley-cum-Quarmby and Lockwood. When the West Riding County Council was formed in 1889, Huddersfield became a <a href="/wiki/County_borough" title="County borough">county borough</a>, exempt from county council control.
</p><p>In 1920, the Corporation bought the Ramsden Estate from the Ramsden family, that had owned much of the town since 1599, for the sum of £1.3&#160;million. As a result, the town became known for a time as 'the town that bought itself'. To this day, much of the freehold of the town belongs to the local authority.<sup id="cite_ref-hudhist_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hudhist-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Huddersfield expanded in 1937, assimilating parts of the <a href="/wiki/Golcar" title="Golcar">Golcar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Linthwaite" title="Linthwaite">Linthwaite</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Crosland" title="South Crosland">South Crosland</a> urban districts.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The county borough was abolished in 1974 and its former area was combined with that of other districts to form the Metropolitan Borough of Kirklees in West Yorkshire.
</p><p>Attempts by the council to gain support for <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city status</a> were rejected by the population in an unofficial referendum held by the <i><a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Daily_Examiner" title="Huddersfield Daily Examiner">Huddersfield Daily Examiner</a></i>. The council did not apply for that status in either the 2000 or 2002 competitions.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Huddersfield had a strong liberal tradition up to the 1950s reflected in the number of liberal social clubs in the town. The current Member of Parliament (MP) for the <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Huddersfield (UK Parliament constituency)">Huddersfield constituency</a> is <a href="/wiki/Barry_Sheerman" title="Barry Sheerman">Barry Sheerman</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Labour_Co-operative" class="mw-redirect" title="Labour Co-operative">Labour Co-operative</a> member.
</p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2001" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2001">United Kingdom Census 2001</a> the population of the Huddersfield urban sub-area of the <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Urban_Area" title="West Yorkshire Urban Area">West Yorkshire Urban Area</a> was 146,234, and the population of the former area of the county borough was 121,620. The wider South Kirklees area had a population of 216,011.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry">Industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Huddersfield is a manufacturing town, despite the university being the largest employer. Historically the town produced woollen textiles. This area of business, along with the chemical and engineering industries that emerged to support the manufacture of textiles, was the basis of the town's nineteenth and early twentieth century prosperity. The number of people who work in textiles has declined greatly, but the surviving companies produce large quantities of <a href="/wiki/Woolen" title="Woolen">woollen</a> products with little labour. The town is home to textile, chemical and engineering companies, including Brook Motors Ltd founded by Ernest Brook in 1904. Against conventional wisdom, he started making <a href="/wiki/Alternating_current" title="Alternating current">alternating current</a> electric motors, and he did this in one room with two assistants and starting capital of just £300. On its 50th anniversary in 1954 it employed more than 2,000 people and, with Ernest's sons Frank and Jack in charge, was the largest exclusive producer of AC motors in the world, and had a turnover of £4,500,000. That same year Brook Motors Ltd operated 10 factories in Huddersfield, its biggest being Empress Works on St Thomas's Road, and opened one at Barugh Green, Barnsley. Other local manufacturers are <a href="/wiki/Cummins" title="Cummins">Cummins Turbo Technologies</a>, founded in 1952 as Holset by Messrs. Holmes and Croset.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> (turbochargers), David Brown Gear systems (industrial gearing), Huddersfield Fine Worsteds (textiles), Taylor &amp; Lodge (textiles), C &amp; J Antich (textiles), Syngenta AG (<a href="/wiki/Agrichemical" class="mw-redirect" title="Agrichemical">agro-chemicals</a>), <a href="/wiki/Pennine_Radio_Limited" title="Pennine Radio Limited">Pennine Radio Limited</a> (<a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronics</a> <a href="/wiki/Transformer" title="Transformer">transformers</a> and sheet <a href="/wiki/Metalworking" title="Metalworking">metalworking</a>) and a large number of niche manufacturers, such as Dual Seal Glass (maker of spandrel glass panels<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>) and Ellis Furniture (producer of kitchen and bathroom furniture).<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Huddersfield is home to Andrew Jones Pies, a regional award-winning pie-maker, and <a href="/wiki/Mamas_and_Papas" class="mw-redirect" title="Mamas and Papas">Mamas and Papas</a>, a manufacturer and retailer of prams, pushchairs and related items and specialist pneumatics supplier Shelley Automation Ltd. 
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_and_television_productions">Film and television productions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Film and television productions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several films and television series have been filmed in and around the town.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> For example, portions of the BBC television series <i><a href="/wiki/Happy_Valley_(TV_series)" title="Happy Valley (TV series)">Happy Valley</a></i> were filmed in Huddersfield; in addition to exteriors, some of the studio filming was done at North Light Film Studios at Brookes Mill, Huddersfield. As well, interiors for the BBC's <i><a href="/wiki/Jamaica_Inn_(2014_TV_series)" title="Jamaica Inn (2014 TV series)">Jamaica Inn</a></i>, for the BBC's <i><a href="/wiki/Remember_Me_(TV_series)" title="Remember Me (TV series)">Remember Me</a></i> and for ITV series <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Work" title="Black Work">Black Work</a></i>, were also filmed at the studios.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> More recently, many of the exteriors of the BBC series <i><a href="/wiki/Jericho_(2016_TV_series)" title="Jericho (2016 TV series)">Jericho</a></i> were filmed at the nearby Rockingstone Quarry and some interior work was done at North Light Film Studios.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The long running <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> comedy show <a href="/wiki/Last_Of_The_Summer_Wine" class="mw-redirect" title="Last Of The Summer Wine">Last Of The Summer Wine</a> was filmed nearby, predominately in the <a href="/wiki/Holme_Valley" title="Holme Valley">Holme Valley</a> around <a href="/wiki/Holmfirth" title="Holmfirth">Holmfirth</a> but also some parts of the <a href="/wiki/Colne_Valley" title="Colne Valley">Colne Valley</a> including <a href="/wiki/Marsden,_West_Yorkshire" title="Marsden, West Yorkshire">Marsden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slaithwaite" title="Slaithwaite">Slaithwaite</a> <sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Huddersfield is located on the valleys of the <a href="/wiki/River_Colne,_West_Yorkshire" title="River Colne, West Yorkshire">River Colne</a> and the <a href="/wiki/River_Holme" title="River Holme">River Holme</a> the confluence of which is located south of the town centre. The town is located in the eastern foothills of the <a href="/wiki/Pennines" title="Pennines">Pennines</a> which extend into the moorlands of the <a href="/wiki/South_Pennines" title="South Pennines">South Pennines</a> west of the town.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Huddersfield experiences a temperate <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> which is relatively mild for its latitude, and which is not subject to extremes of temperature because of the moderating influence of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>, Huddersfield is certified as <i>Cfb</i>.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Divisions_and_suburbs">Divisions and suburbs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Divisions and suburbs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After boundary changes in 2004, Huddersfield now covers eight of the twenty-three <a href="/wiki/Ward_(country_subdivision)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ward (country subdivision)">electoral wards</a> for Kirklees Council. Neighbouring wards in the <a href="/wiki/Colne_Valley" title="Colne Valley">Colne Valley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holme_Valley" title="Holme Valley">Holme Valley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kirkburton" title="Kirkburton">Kirkburton</a> are often considered to be part of Huddersfield though they are predominantly <a href="/wiki/Rural" class="mw-redirect" title="Rural">semi-rural</a>. Huddersfield town centre is located within the Newsome ward. The eight wards that make up Huddersfield proper, with their populations, areas and constituent suburbs (mid-year 2005 estimates) are:
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_belt">Green belt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Green belt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/South_and_West_Yorkshire_Green_Belt" title="South and West Yorkshire Green Belt">South and West Yorkshire Green Belt</a></div>
<p>Huddersfield is within a <a href="/wiki/Green_belt_(United_Kingdom)" title="Green belt (United Kingdom)">green belt</a> region that extends into the Kirklees borough and wider surrounding counties. It is in place to reduce <a href="/wiki/Urban_sprawl" title="Urban sprawl">urban sprawl</a>, prevent the towns in the <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Urban_Area" title="West Yorkshire Urban Area">West Yorkshire Urban Area</a> conurbation from further convergence, protect the identity of outlying communities, encourage <a href="/wiki/Brownfield" class="mw-redirect" title="Brownfield">brownfield</a> reuse, and preserve nearby countryside. This is achieved by restricting inappropriate development within the designated areas, and imposing stricter conditions on permitted building.<sup id="cite_ref-belt1_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-belt1-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The green belt surrounds the Huddersfield built-up area, separating towns and villages throughout the borough. Larger outlying communities such as Upper Hopton, Grange Moor, Highburton, <a href="/wiki/Farnley_Tyas" title="Farnley Tyas">Farnley Tyas</a>, Netherton, <a href="/wiki/Honley" title="Honley">Honley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Outlane" title="Outlane">Outlane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slaithwaite" title="Slaithwaite">Slaithwaite</a>, Wellhouse are also exempt from the green belt area. However, nearby smaller villages, hamlets and rural areas such as Thurgory, <a href="/wiki/Gawthorpe,_Kirklees" title="Gawthorpe, Kirklees">Gawthorpe Green</a>, Bog Green, Upper Heaton, <a href="/wiki/Wilberlee" title="Wilberlee">Wilberlee</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Crosland" title="South Crosland">South Crosland</a>, Rushfield Bridge, and Bank End are 'washed over' by the designation. Much semi-rural land on the fringes is also included. The green belt was defined from the 1960s,<sup id="cite_ref-belt1_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-belt1-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> and the total area in Kirklees amounted to some 23,050 hectares (230.5&#160;km<sup>2</sup>; 89.0&#160;sq&#160;mi) (2017, excluding the Peak District National Park),<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> 70% of the borough.<sup id="cite_ref-belt1_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-belt1-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A subsidiary aim of the green belt is to encourage recreation and leisure interests,<sup id="cite_ref-belt1_33-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-belt1-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> with nearby rural landscape features, greenfield areas and facilities including <a href="/wiki/Castle_Hill,_Huddersfield" title="Castle Hill, Huddersfield">Castle Hill</a> with Victoria Tower; Coal Pit Scrog and Hall Wood in Lepton; Blackmoorfoot reservoir; Longwood reservoir; Huddersfield Narrow Canal and the River Colne west of the town; River Holme south of the town; <a href="/wiki/Storthes_Hall" title="Storthes Hall">Storthes Hall</a>; Kirkheaton cricket ground; and Beaumont Park. Further afield west of <a href="/wiki/Marsden,_West_Yorkshire" title="Marsden, West Yorkshire">Marsden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meltham" title="Meltham">Meltham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Holmbridge" title="Holmbridge">Holmbridge</a>, the green belt also borders the <a href="/wiki/Peak_District_National_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Peak District National Park">Peak District National Park</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnicity">Ethnicity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Ethnicity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Like many former <a href="/wiki/Mill_town" title="Mill town">mill towns</a>, Huddersfield has a higher than average number of residents from <a href="/wiki/Minority_group" title="Minority group">ethnic minorities</a>. The white population makes up 81% of the population comparing to 91.3% for England as a whole (2001). The largest ethnic minority group are those who have described themselves as being <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asian</a> or <a href="/wiki/British_Asian" title="British Asian">British Asian</a> originating from the Indian sub-continent (<a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>) with 10,837, or 8.9% (compared to 7.8% for England as a whole (2011). An ethnicity summary of the town's 121,620 population is 98,454 (81.0%) white, 15,072 (12.4%) Asian or British Asian, 4,328 (3.6%) Black or <a href="/wiki/Black_British" title="Black British">Black British</a>, 328 (0.3%), 259 (0.2%) Other and 3,131 (2.6%) Mixed.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, Huddersfield had a population of 162,949 and was 75.8% White (which includes people from Ireland, Mainland Europe and other places), 72.1% White British (or 117,548 people), 14.9% Asian (24,201 people) and 4.2% Black (6,822 people).<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Huddersfield is slightly above the English average for those who have no religion and also for the number of <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a>. Conversely, it is below average for its number of Christians.
</p><p>There are a number of Churches, <a href="/wiki/Gurdwara" title="Gurdwara">Gurdwaras</a>, Mosques and Temples covering a wide spectrum of religions in the Huddersfield area. These include established Christian denominations, such as the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Baptist" class="mw-redirect" title="Baptist">Baptist</a> Church, <a href="/wiki/Methodism" title="Methodism">Methodism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Presbyterianism" title="Presbyterianism">Presbyterianism</a> and the <a href="/wiki/St_Patrick%27s_Church,_Huddersfield" title="St Patrick&#39;s Church, Huddersfield">Roman Catholic Church</a>. Religions that are relatively new to Britain also have places of worship in the town: <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mormonism" title="Mormonism">Mormonism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a> all have congregational buildings.
</p>
