<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks_and_architecture">Landmarks and architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Landmarks and architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Victoria_Tower_Castle_Hill(RLH).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Victoria_Tower_Castle_Hill%28RLH%29.jpg/170px-Victoria_Tower_Castle_Hill%28RLH%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Victoria_Tower_Castle_Hill%28RLH%29.jpg/255px-Victoria_Tower_Castle_Hill%28RLH%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Victoria_Tower_Castle_Hill%28RLH%29.jpg/340px-Victoria_Tower_Castle_Hill%28RLH%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="429" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Victoria_Tower_Castle_Hill(RLH).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Victoria Tower at 'Castle Hill'</div></div></div>
<p>Huddersfield has an abundance of <a href="/wiki/Victorian_architecture" title="Victorian architecture">Victorian architecture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The most conspicuous landmark is the <a href="/wiki/Castle_Hill,_Huddersfield#Victoria_Tower" title="Castle Hill, Huddersfield">Victoria Tower</a> on Castle Hill. Overlooking the town, the tower was constructed to mark <a href="/wiki/Victoria_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria of the United Kingdom">Queen Victoria's</a> 60th Jubilee Year. A picture of the Victoria Tower features on the <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> wine <i>Castle Hill</i>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Town_Hall_and_Concert_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_321863.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Town_Hall_and_Concert_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_321863.jpg/220px-Town_Hall_and_Concert_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_321863.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Town_Hall_and_Concert_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_321863.jpg/330px-Town_Hall_and_Concert_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_321863.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Town_Hall_and_Concert_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_321863.jpg/440px-Town_Hall_and_Concert_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_321863.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Town_Hall_and_Concert_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_321863.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Huddersfield Town Hall</div></div></div>
<p>Huddersfield Town Hall was designed by John H. Abbey and built in two stages between 1875 and 1881. The first section opened on 26 June 1878, comprising the Mayor's Parlour, Council Chamber, Reception Room and municipal offices including the Sanitary Inspector, Inspector of Weights and Measures, Medical Officer, Town Clerk, Borough Surveyor and the Rates Office. The second phase opened in October 1881 comprising the Magistrates' Court and Concert Hall. The hall seats up to 1,200 people and hosts events ranging from classical to comedy and from choral to community events.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Colonnade" title="Colonnade">colonnaded</a> <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_railway_station" title="Huddersfield railway station">Huddersfield railway station</a> in St George's Square was once described as 'a <a href="/wiki/Stately_home" class="mw-redirect" title="Stately home">stately home</a> with trains in it', and by <a href="/wiki/Nikolaus_Pevsner" title="Nikolaus Pevsner">Sir Nikolaus Pevsner</a> as "one of the best early railway stations in England".<sup id="cite_ref-pevsner_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pevsner-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> A bronze statue of Huddersfield-born Sir <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a>, Prime Minister 1964–1970 and 1974–1976 stands in front of its entrance.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/George_Hotel,_Huddersfield" title="George Hotel, Huddersfield">George Hotel</a> designed by <a href="/wiki/William_Wallen_(architect)" title="William Wallen (architect)">William Wallen</a> was built by Wallen and Charles Child in 1850. The hotel's Italianate façade became Huddersfield's adopted architectural style as the town developed over following decade.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_church_of_St_Peter_-_Kirkgate_-_geograph.org.uk_-_351683.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/The_church_of_St_Peter_-_Kirkgate_-_geograph.org.uk_-_351683.jpg/220px-The_church_of_St_Peter_-_Kirkgate_-_geograph.org.uk_-_351683.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/The_church_of_St_Peter_-_Kirkgate_-_geograph.org.uk_-_351683.jpg/330px-The_church_of_St_Peter_-_Kirkgate_-_geograph.org.uk_-_351683.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/The_church_of_St_Peter_-_Kirkgate_-_geograph.org.uk_-_351683.jpg/440px-The_church_of_St_Peter_-_Kirkgate_-_geograph.org.uk_-_351683.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_church_of_St_Peter_-_Kirkgate_-_geograph.org.uk_-_351683.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/St_Peter%27s_Church,_Huddersfield" title="St Peter&#39;s Church, Huddersfield">St Peter's Church</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/St_Peter%27s_Church,_Huddersfield" title="St Peter&#39;s Church, Huddersfield">St Peter's Church</a> (Huddersfield <a href="/wiki/Parish_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Parish Church">Parish Church</a>) is situated on a site that dates back to the 11th century and is adjacent to the town centre, on Byram Street near the Pack Horse Centre. The current church on the site was constructed in 1838, making it somewhat newer than <a href="/wiki/Holy_Trinity_Church,_Huddersfield" title="Holy Trinity Church, Huddersfield">Holy Trinity Church</a>, just outside the town centre and constructed between 1816 and 1819.
</p><p>The Pack Horse Centre is a covered <a href="/wiki/Pedestrianised" class="mw-redirect" title="Pedestrianised">pedestrianised</a> shopping area constructed over a <a href="/wiki/Cobblestone" title="Cobblestone">cobblestone</a> street, Pack Horse Yard, renamed Pack Horse Walk. <a href="/wiki/Pack_horse" class="mw-redirect" title="Pack horse">Pack horses</a> carried merchandise over pack-horse routes across the <a href="/wiki/Pennines" title="Pennines">Pennines</a> before <a href="/wiki/Toll_road" title="Toll road">turnpike</a> roads and railways improved transportation. The pedestrian link passes from Kirkgate, across King Street and along Victoria Lane, by the Shambles, to the Piazza and the distinctive market hall at Queensgate, which was built to replace the old Shambles Market Hall in the early 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Next to the Piazza is the Victorian town hall and the 1930s public library.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Beaumont_Park" title="Beaumont Park">Beaumont Park</a> about 2 miles (3.2&#160;km) to the south of the town centre was bequeathed to the town in the 1880s, by Henry Frederick Beaumont ('Beaumont's of Whitley' estate) and was opened on 13 October 1883, by <a href="/wiki/Prince_Leopold,_Duke_of_Albany" title="Prince Leopold, Duke of Albany">Prince Leopold</a>, fourth son of <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a>, and his wife <a href="/wiki/Princess_Helena_of_Waldeck_and_Pyrmont" title="Princess Helena of Waldeck and Pyrmont">Princess Helena of Waldeck and Pyrmont</a> (Duke and Duchess of Albany). It is a fine example of a <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian era</a> public park with water cascades, bandstand and woodland.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/St_Paul%27s_Street_drill_hall,_Huddersfield" title="St Paul&#39;s Street drill hall, Huddersfield">St Paul's Street drill hall</a> was designed by Captain Willey Cooper and completed in 1901.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Greenhead_Park" title="Greenhead Park">Greenhead Park</a> is another large park in Huddersfield, situated around 0.4 miles (0.64&#160;km) west of the town centre. A multimillion-pound restoration project, funded by the Heritage Lottery fund<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> was finished in autumn 2012.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Huddersfieldmap_1954.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Huddersfieldmap_1954.png/220px-Huddersfieldmap_1954.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Huddersfieldmap_1954.png/330px-Huddersfieldmap_1954.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Huddersfieldmap_1954.png/440px-Huddersfieldmap_1954.png 2x" data-file-width="2781" data-file-height="2393" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Huddersfieldmap_1954.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Huddersfield from 1954</div></div></div>
<p>Huddersfield is connected to the national motorway network via the <a href="/wiki/M1_motorway" title="M1 motorway">M1</a> and <a href="/wiki/M62_motorway" title="M62 motorway">M62</a> motorways. The M1 passes about 10 miles (16&#160;km) to the east. The M62 passes about 2.5 miles (4.0&#160;km) to the north and Huddersfield is served by three junctions: Mount (<a href="/wiki/A640_road" title="A640 road">A640</a>, J23 – limited access), Ainley Top (<a href="/wiki/A629_road" title="A629 road">A629</a>, J24) and between <a href="/wiki/Brighouse" title="Brighouse">Brighouse</a> and Cooper Bridge (<a href="/wiki/A644_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A644 road">A644</a>, J25).
</p><p>Huddersfield Corporation built an inner <a href="/wiki/Ring_road" title="Ring road">ring road</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/A62_road" title="A62 road">A62</a>, in the 1970s. The area within the ring road now defines the town's central business district. The ring road relieves traffic congestion in the town centre where many roads are <a href="/wiki/Pedestrianised" class="mw-redirect" title="Pedestrianised">pedestrianised</a>.
</p><p>Main routes into Huddersfield include the A62 Leeds Road, <a href="/wiki/A641_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A641 road">A641</a> Bradford Road, A629 Halifax Road – Penistone Road, A640 New Hey Road and the A62 Manchester Road.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hudds-ftb.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Hudds-ftb.jpg/220px-Hudds-ftb.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Hudds-ftb.jpg/330px-Hudds-ftb.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Hudds-ftb.jpg/440px-Hudds-ftb.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hudds-ftb.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Huddersfield Free Town Bus</div></div></div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Huddersfield" title="Trolleybuses in Huddersfield">trolleybus system</a> operated from 1933 to 1968. <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_bus_station" title="Huddersfield bus station">Huddersfield bus station</a> was opened by the Mayor, Councillor Mernagh on 26 March 1974, although it had not been completed.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> It is the busiest bus station in West Yorkshire with a daily footfall of almost 35,000. Most bus services pass through the bus station. Many services are subsidised by Metro.
</p><p>Huddersfield's bus operators reflect the national situation; local subsidiaries of three dominant national operators provide most services in the area: <a href="/wiki/First_Calderdale_%26_Huddersfield" title="First Calderdale &amp; Huddersfield">First Calderdale &amp; Huddersfield</a> provide most local services in Huddersfield and some services outside Kirklees with destinations including Bradford, Brighouse, Halifax, Manchester and <a href="/wiki/Oldham" title="Oldham">Oldham</a>. <a href="/wiki/Arriva_Yorkshire" title="Arriva Yorkshire">Arriva Yorkshire</a> provide frequent services to Dewsbury and Leeds, and <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Tiger" title="Yorkshire Tiger">Yorkshire Tiger</a> provide almost all services in the south east of the town. Other smaller operators include <a href="/wiki/Stotts_Coaches" title="Stotts Coaches">Stotts Coaches</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Tiger#Tiger_Blue" title="Yorkshire Tiger">Tiger Blue</a>. Centrebus Holdings purchased Teamdeck in May 2008, along with <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_Yorkshire" title="Stagecoach Yorkshire">Stagecoach Yorkshire</a>'s Huddersfield depot.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In November 2006, a <a href="/wiki/Zero-fare_public_transport" class="mw-redirect" title="Zero-fare public transport">zero-fare</a> town centre bus service, the <a href="/wiki/FreeCityBus" title="FreeCityBus">Free Town Bus</a>, was launched run by K-Line in partnership with Kirklees Council and Metro. Today this is run by <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Tiger" title="Yorkshire Tiger">Yorkshire Tiger</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_railway_station" title="Huddersfield railway station">Huddersfield railway station</a> has a comprehensive local and regional rail service but there is no direct service to London, and passengers have to change at <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Piccadilly railway station">Manchester Piccadilly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wakefield_Westgate_railway_station" title="Wakefield Westgate railway station">Wakefield Westgate</a> or <a href="/wiki/Mirfield_railway_station" title="Mirfield railway station">Mirfield</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Some services are subsidised by the public transport coordinator, <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Metro" title="West Yorkshire Metro">West Yorkshire Metro</a>. A frequent express service operates to <a href="/wiki/Dewsbury_railway_station" title="Dewsbury railway station">Dewsbury</a>, Leeds and Manchester and regular services to <a href="/wiki/Darlington_railway_station" title="Darlington railway station">Darlington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hull_Paragon_Interchange" title="Hull Paragon Interchange">Hull</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station" title="Liverpool Lime Street railway station">Liverpool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Airport railway station">Manchester Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_railway_station" title="Middlesbrough railway station">Middlesbrough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_railway_station" title="Newcastle railway station">Newcastle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scarborough_railway_station" title="Scarborough railway station">Scarborough</a> and <a href="/wiki/York_railway_station" title="York railway station">York</a> operated by <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a>. There are local stopping services operated by <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a> linking Huddersfield with <a href="/wiki/Barnsley_Interchange" title="Barnsley Interchange">Barnsley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bradford_Interchange" title="Bradford Interchange">Bradford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brighouse_railway_station" title="Brighouse railway station">Brighouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dewsbury" title="Dewsbury">Dewsbury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Halifax_railway_station_(England)" title="Halifax railway station (England)">Halifax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield railway station">Sheffield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wakefield_Kirkgate_railway_station" title="Wakefield Kirkgate railway station">Wakefield</a>.
</p>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:802px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Huddersfield_Railway_Station_(RLH).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Huddersfield_Railway_Station_%28RLH%29.jpg/800px-Huddersfield_Railway_Station_%28RLH%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="800" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Huddersfield_Railway_Station_%28RLH%29.jpg/1200px-Huddersfield_Railway_Station_%28RLH%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Huddersfield_Railway_Station_%28RLH%29.jpg/1600px-Huddersfield_Railway_Station_%28RLH%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6777" data-file-height="1996" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Huddersfield_Railway_Station_(RLH).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_railway_station" title="Huddersfield railway station">Huddersfield railway station</a> in St George's Square</div></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canal">Canal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Canal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Broad_Canal" title="Huddersfield Broad Canal">Huddersfield Broad Canal</a>, originally the Sir John Ramsden Canal, and the <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Narrow_Canal" title="Huddersfield Narrow Canal">Huddersfield Narrow Canal</a> which are both navigable by <a href="/wiki/Narrowboat" title="Narrowboat">narrowboat</a>, and the broad canal by wider craft, wind around the south side of town. To the rear of the <a href="/wiki/YMCA" title="YMCA">YMCA</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Turnbridge" title="Turnbridge">Turnbridge</a> section is an electrically operated road bridge, which is still in use, to raise the road and allow boat traffic to pass. This bridge originally used a <a href="/wiki/Windlass" title="Windlass">windlass</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Huddersfield_002.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Huddersfield_002.jpg/220px-Huddersfield_002.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Huddersfield_002.jpg/330px-Huddersfield_002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Huddersfield_002.jpg/440px-Huddersfield_002.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Huddersfield_002.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/John_Smith%27s_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="John Smith&#39;s Stadium">John Smith's Stadium</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> are the main spectator sports in Huddersfield. Its professional football team, <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Town_A.F.C." title="Huddersfield Town A.F.C.">Huddersfield Town A.F.C.</a> play in the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Championship">Championship</a> after 2 seasons in the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>. In 1926, the club became the first in England to win three successive league titles, a feat only three other clubs have matched.
</p><p>The town was the birthplace of rugby league, and is home to the <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Giants" title="Huddersfield Giants">Huddersfield Giants</a> who play in the <a href="/wiki/Super_League" title="Super League">Super League</a>, the top division in Europe. The town is home to <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Underbank_Rangers" class="mw-redirect" title="Huddersfield Underbank Rangers">Huddersfield Underbank Rangers</a> rugby league club, who play in the Rugby League Conference.
<a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Rugby_Union_Football_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Huddersfield Rugby Union Football Club">Huddersfield Rugby Union Football Club</a> play in the <a href="/wiki/National_Division_Three_North" class="mw-redirect" title="National Division Three North">National Division Three North</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Y.M.C.A._RUFC" title="Huddersfield Y.M.C.A. RUFC">Huddersfield Y.M.C.A. RUFC</a> who play in <a href="/wiki/North_1_East" title="North 1 East">North 1 East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Rams_Aussie_Rules" class="mw-redirect" title="Huddersfield Rams Aussie Rules">Huddersfield Rams Aussie Rules</a> club. The main sporting arena is <a href="/wiki/John_Smith%27s_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="John Smith&#39;s Stadium">John Smith's Stadium</a>, home to both the football team and rugby league side. Also within the town boundaries is <a href="/wiki/AFC_Emley" class="mw-redirect" title="AFC Emley">AFC Emley</a> who were formed when the original <a href="/wiki/Wakefield_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Wakefield FC">Emley FC</a> left for Wakefield.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rugby_football">Rugby football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Rugby football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Rugby was first played in the town in 1848 and the Huddersfield Athletic Club, the direct progenitors of Huddersfield Giants, formed in 1864, played its first rugby game in 1866. In Huddersfield on 29 August 1895, 22 northern clubs met in the <a href="/wiki/George_Hotel,_Huddersfield" title="George Hotel, Huddersfield">George Hotel</a> and voted to <a href="/wiki/Secession" title="Secession">secede</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_Union" title="Rugby Football Union">Rugby Football Union</a> and set up the 'Northern Rugby Football Union' which became the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_League" title="Rugby Football League">Rugby Football League</a> in 1922. The <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_Heritage_Centre" title="Rugby League Heritage Centre">Rugby League Heritage Centre</a> is in the basement of the George Hotel.
</p><p>Following the split of 1895, Huddersfield became a focus for rugby league and is represented by Huddersfield Giants in the Super League. <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Giants" title="Huddersfield Giants">Huddersfield Giants</a>, the town's rugby league club, has won the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_League_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby Football League Championship">Rugby Football League Championship</a> seven times, most recently in 1961–62, and the <a href="/wiki/Challenge_Cup" title="Challenge Cup">Challenge Cup</a> six times, the last time in 1952–53.
</p><p>After 1895 rugby was played exclusively under the auspices of the Northern Rugby Football Union until 1909 when Huddersfield Old Boys were formed to play under <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> rules, playing nomadically at five grounds until buying farmland at Waterloo in 1919 and, in 1946, renaming the club <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Rugby_Union_Football_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Huddersfield Rugby Union Football Club">Huddersfield RUFC</a>. In 1969 the club was at the forefront of a revolution in English rugby when it became the first club in the country to organise mini and junior rugby teams. The innovation spread and almost every club in the country has a thriving junior section providing a production-line of home-grown talent. Junior players at Huddersfield number over 200. In 1997 the Waterloo junior grounds were sold and the 26-acre (0.11&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) former <a href="/wiki/Bass_Brewery" title="Bass Brewery">Bass Brewery</a> site at Lockwood Park was purchased for its replacement. With the assistance of a £2&#160;million grant from <a href="/wiki/Sport_England" title="Sport England">Sport England</a>, the club has transformed it into a major sports complex, conference centre and business park.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Association_football">Association football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Association football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Town_F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Huddersfield Town F.C.">Huddersfield Town F.C.</a> is the town's senior association football team, founded in 1908, and currently playing in the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Championship">Championship</a>.
In 1921–22 Huddersfield won the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> and between 1923 and 1926 became the first club to win the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">League Championship</a> three times in a row, an achievement matched only by three other teams. After several decades in lower divisions, Huddersfield Town FC returned to top flight football in 2017 when the club entered the Premier League for the first time. The club left its ground at <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Road,_Huddersfield" class="mw-redirect" title="Leeds Road, Huddersfield">Leeds Road</a> in 1994 and now shares the <a href="/wiki/John_Smith%27s_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="John Smith&#39;s Stadium">John Smith's Stadium</a> with the Huddersfield Giants rugby league team.
</p><p>Notable ex-players include Scottish international <a href="/wiki/Denis_Law" title="Denis Law">Denis Law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ray_Wilson_(English_footballer)" title="Ray Wilson (English footballer)">Ray Wilson</a>, a <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a> winner with <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> in 1966 and <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Cherry" title="Trevor Cherry">Trevor Cherry</a>, England international.
<a href="/wiki/Herbert_Chapman" title="Herbert Chapman">Herbert Chapman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Shankly" title="Bill Shankly">Bill Shankly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neil_Warnock" title="Neil Warnock">Neil Warnock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Bruce" title="Steve Bruce">Steve Bruce</a> are notable former Huddersfield Town managers.
</p><p>There are also 3 semi professional clubs within the town, <a href="/wiki/Emley_A.F.C." title="Emley A.F.C.">Emley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shelley_Community_F.C." title="Shelley Community F.C.">Shelley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Golcar_United_F.C." title="Golcar United F.C.">Golcar Utd</a> who, from the 2019–20 season will all play in the <a href="/wiki/North_West_Counties_Football_League" title="North West Counties Football League">North West Counties Football League</a> Division One North
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_sports">Other sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Other sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Rams_Aussie_Rules" class="mw-redirect" title="Huddersfield Rams Aussie Rules">Huddersfield Rams Aussie Rules</a> is an Australian rules football team, formed in 2008. The club played its first season in 2009 and won the <a href="/wiki/Aussie_Rules_UK" title="Aussie Rules UK">Aussie Rules UK</a> National League – Central Division and took part in the North West Division in 2010.
</p><p>Huddersfield has a number of field <a href="/wiki/Hockey" title="Hockey">hockey</a> teams, many of which train at the Lockwood Park sports complex on the all-weather pitch.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Motorcycle_speedway" title="Motorcycle speedway">Motorcycle speedway</a> racing was staged in Huddersfield in the UK pioneer year of 1928. A venue in the town staged four or five meetings.
<a href="/wiki/James_Whitham" title="James Whitham">James Whitham</a>, is a former 'British <a href="/wiki/Superbike_racing" title="Superbike racing">Superbike</a> Champion'. Lepton born <a href="/wiki/Tom_Sykes" title="Tom Sykes">Tom Sykes</a> joined the Yamaha Motor Italia World team in the 2009 World Superbike season<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> after spells in British Supersports &amp; <a href="/wiki/British_Superbike_Championship" title="British Superbike Championship">British Superbikes</a> in which he finished 4th in the 2009 Season. He won his first race in <a href="/wiki/Superbike_World_Championship" title="Superbike World Championship">World Superbikes</a> in one of two wildcard meetings.
</p><p>On 6 July 2014, Stage 2 of the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Tour_de_France" title="Tour de France">Tour de France</a> from York to Sheffield passed through the town.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Huddersfield%22">"Huddersfield"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Huddersfield%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Huddersfield%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Huddersfield%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Huddersfield%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Huddersfield%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2018</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Huddersfield_Library_and_Art_Gallery.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Huddersfield_Library_and_Art_Gallery.jpg/220px-Huddersfield_Library_and_Art_Gallery.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Huddersfield_Library_and_Art_Gallery.jpg/330px-Huddersfield_Library_and_Art_Gallery.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Huddersfield_Library_and_Art_Gallery.jpg/440px-Huddersfield_Library_and_Art_Gallery.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="1728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Huddersfield_Library_and_Art_Gallery.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Huddersfield Library and Art Gallery</div></div></div>
<p>Huddersfield Choral Society founded in 1836, claims to be the UK's leading <a href="/wiki/Choir" title="Choir">choral society</a>. Its history was chronicled in the book<i> 'And The Glory'</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> written to commemorate the society's 150th anniversary in 1986 – its title derived from a line in the <a href="/wiki/The_Hallelujah_Chorus" class="mw-redirect" title="The Hallelujah Chorus">Hallelujah Chorus</a> featuring in <a href="/wiki/George_Frideric_Handel" title="George Frideric Handel">Handel's</a> landmark choral arrangement <i><a href="/wiki/Messiah_(Handel)" title="Messiah (Handel)">Messiah</a></i>.
</p><p>The annual <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Contemporary_Music_Festival" title="Huddersfield Contemporary Music Festival">Huddersfield Contemporary Music Festival</a> is held in the town which is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="Huddersfield Philharmonic Orchestra">Huddersfield Philharmonic Orchestra</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Singers" title="Huddersfield Singers">Huddersfield Singers</a>.
</p><p>On Christmas Day 1977, the <a href="/wiki/Sex_Pistols" title="Sex Pistols">Sex Pistols</a> played their last two British shows, a matinee for the children of striking firefighters, at Ivanhoe's nightclub, before embarking on their ill-fated US tour which saw the group's acrimonious collapse. In the early-mid-1990s, Flex, an underground Jungle/<a href="/wiki/Drum_and_bass" title="Drum and bass">Drum 'n' Bass</a> record label, was founded by musician and <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1Xtra" title="BBC Radio 1Xtra">BBC Radio 1Xtra</a> DJ, L Double. In 2000 another independent record label Chocolate Fireguard Records was founded by singer Pat Fulgoni who developed a three-stage community music event, <a href="/wiki/Timeless_Festival" title="Timeless Festival">Timeless Festival</a>, in Ravensknowle Park, featuring a range of electronica, <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" title="Hip hop">hip hop</a> and rock music.
</p><p>There are other annual music festivals held in the town and surrounding area, examples being the <a href="/wiki/Marsden,_West_Yorkshire" title="Marsden, West Yorkshire">Marsden</a> <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">Jazz</a> Festival,<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Mrs Sunderland,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Janet Beaumont, the <a href="/wiki/Holmfirth" title="Holmfirth">Holmfirth</a> Festivals, and the Haydn Wood (Linthwaite). The Haydn Wood (for under 21s) and Mrs Sunderland festival focus on musical and oratorial performance. The Mrs Sunderland Music festival is the second oldest in the United Kingdom, started in 1889 lasting for nine days each year. Free music concerts have been put on for the town, including bands such as the Ordinary Boys, the Script and Elliott Minor. There are many local choirs, youth and adult, a noted example of the latter being the <a href="/wiki/Honley" title="Honley">Honley</a> Male Voice Choir.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Home-grown musical talent of all kinds is complemented by the student intake to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Huddersfield" title="University of Huddersfield">University of Huddersfield</a>'s music department. "The Sheriff of Huddersfield" is a song by heavy metal band <a href="/wiki/Iron_Maiden" title="Iron Maiden">Iron Maiden</a> on the B-side of their 1986 single "<a href="/wiki/Wasted_Years" title="Wasted Years">Wasted Years</a>", written about their co-manager <a href="/wiki/Rod_Smallwood" title="Rod Smallwood">Rod Smallwood</a>, leaving his home town of Huddersfield and struggling to settle into life in Los Angeles. Huddersfield is home to <a href="/wiki/Thrash_metal" title="Thrash metal">thrash metal</a> band <a href="/wiki/Evile" title="Evile">Evile</a>, dance rock outfit <a href="/wiki/Kava_Kava_(band)" title="Kava Kava (band)">Kava Kava</a>, the birthplace of the synthpop musician <a href="/wiki/Billy_Currie" title="Billy Currie">Billy Currie</a> (of <a href="/wiki/Ultravox" title="Ultravox">Ultravox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Visage_(band)" title="Visage (band)">Visage</a>), the hard rock bassist <a href="/wiki/John_McCoy_(musician)" title="John McCoy (musician)">John McCoy</a> who played with <a href="/wiki/Neo_(UK_band)" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo (UK band)">Neo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gillan_(band)" title="Gillan (band)">Gillan</a>.
</p><p>Long-running television series have been filmed in and around Huddersfield. They include <i><a href="/wiki/Last_of_the_Summer_Wine" title="Last of the Summer Wine">Last of the Summer Wine</a></i>, which is usually associated with <a href="/wiki/Holmfirth" title="Holmfirth">Holmfirth</a>, but uses locations in the Holme and Colne valleys; <i><a href="/wiki/Where_the_Heart_Is_(1997_TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Where the Heart Is (1997 TV series)">Where the Heart Is</a></i> was filmed in the Colne valley around <a href="/wiki/Slaithwaite" title="Slaithwaite">Slaithwaite</a>; <i>Wokenwell</i> was shot on location in the Colne Valley and <a href="/wiki/Marsden,_West_Yorkshire" title="Marsden, West Yorkshire">Marsden</a>; and <i><a href="/wiki/The_League_of_Gentlemen" title="The League of Gentlemen">The League of Gentlemen</a></i> used locations around Marsden. The feature films <i><a href="/wiki/Between_Two_Women_(2000_film)" title="Between Two Women (2000 film)">Between Two Women</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jealous_God" title="The Jealous God">The Jealous God</a></i> were filmed in and around Huddersfield.
</p><p>Huddersfield Art Gallery occupies the top floor of the library building on Princess Alexandra Walk, it houses an extensive collection of work by internationally renowned artists such as <a href="/wiki/Francis_Bacon" title="Francis Bacon">Francis Bacon</a>, <a href="/wiki/L.S._Lowry" class="mw-redirect" title="L.S. Lowry">L.S. Lowry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Henry_Moore" title="Henry Moore">Henry Moore</a>, as well as significant regional artists. Throughout the year, it holds exhibitions of work by both established and emerging artists.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Denimu" title="Denimu">Ian Berry</a> was born in Netherton, Huddersfield and was educated in the town and went to <a href="/wiki/Greenhead_College" title="Greenhead College">Greenhead College</a><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> and is internationally renowned for his art using only <a href="/wiki/Denim" title="Denim">denim</a> <a href="/wiki/Jeans" title="Jeans">jeans</a> and was named as one of the top 30 artists under the world in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> In 1996 aged 11 he won the <i><a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Daily_Examiner" title="Huddersfield Daily Examiner">Huddersfield Daily Examiner</a></i> 125th Birthday competition that saw his design printed on to mugs, tea towels and posters.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_events">Cultural events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Cultural events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Huddersfield Festival of Light takes place annually in December,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> usually in the town centre adjacent to the railway station. Each year there is a performance by a theatre company. The finale is a firework display. The 2007 show was performed by French company Plasticiens Volants, which used large inflatable sea creatures in a parade through the streets as they told the story of 'Pearl'. The 2005 and 2008 performances were by the <a href="/wiki/Valencia" title="Valencia">Valencian</a> artists Xarxa Teatre.
The 2010 festival featured Belgian company Company Tol and their suspension act – Corazon de Angeles (Angels' Heart) and ended on 5 December with fireworks in St. George's Square.
</p><p>Huddersfield has a very well established Saint Patrick's Day Parade held annually.
</p><p>Huddersfield Caribbean Carnival in mid-July, begins with a procession from the Hudawi Cultural Centre in Hillhouse, through the town centre to Greenhead Park where troupes display their costumes on stage. <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> food, fairground rides and various stalls and attractions are available. A "young blud" stage presents Hip Hop, UK garage, RnB and bassline.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Literature_Festival" title="Huddersfield Literature Festival">Huddersfield Literature Festival</a> is held annually in the town,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> and features author events, creative writing classes and poetry nights, and sometimes creative writing competitions.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Present_day">Present day</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Present day">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shopping">Shopping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Shopping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Huddersfield has a large and diverse retail shopping area, enclosed within the town's ring road, compared with other towns of its size. There are three shopping areas: <a href="/wiki/Kingsgate_Shopping_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingsgate Shopping Centre">Kingsgate</a>, The Packhorse Precinct and The Piazza Centre. The Piazza offers an outdoor shopping mall near the public library, with a grassed area, used for relaxation and events throughout the year such as entertainment, international markets and iceskating in winter. Through the adjacent Market Arcade is a covered market hall, which has listed building status, due in part to its distinctive roof formed by <a href="/wiki/Hyperbola" title="Hyperbola">hyperbolic</a> <a href="/wiki/Paraboloid" title="Paraboloid">paraboloids</a>. It is adjacent to the town hall and public library. An open market is located next to <a href="/wiki/Tesco" title="Tesco">Tesco</a>, on the opposite side of the town centre.
</p><p>The town centre is home to several national high street retailers and chain stores including <a href="/wiki/Clinton_Cards" class="mw-redirect" title="Clinton Cards">Clinton Cards</a>, <a href="/wiki/GAME_(retailer)" class="mw-redirect" title="GAME (retailer)">GAME</a>, <a href="/wiki/House_of_Fraser" title="House of Fraser">House of Fraser</a>, <a href="/wiki/JD_Sports" title="JD Sports">JD Sports</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sports_Direct" title="Sports Direct">Sports Direct</a> (formerly JJB), <a href="/wiki/W_H_Smith" class="mw-redirect" title="W H Smith">W H Smiths</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wilko_(retailer)" title="Wilko (retailer)">Wilko</a>; up until January 2008, it also had a <a href="/wiki/Woolworths_Group" title="Woolworths Group">Woolworths</a>. Fast food outlets include <a href="/wiki/KFC" title="KFC">KFC</a>, <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald&#39;s">McDonald's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pizza_Hut" title="Pizza Hut">Pizza Hut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Subway_(restaurant)" title="Subway (restaurant)">Subway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wimpy_Bar" class="mw-redirect" title="Wimpy Bar">Wimpy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nando%27s" title="Nando&#39;s">Nando's</a>. High street clothing and fashion retail outlets such as, <a href="/wiki/Marks_%26_Spencer" title="Marks &amp; Spencer">Marks &amp; Spencer</a>, <a href="/wiki/River_Island" title="River Island">River Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Topman" title="Topman">Topman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Next_(clothing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Next (clothing)">Next</a>. There are three major supermarket outlets located in the town centre, and alongside the ring road: two <a href="/wiki/Sainsbury%27s" title="Sainsbury&#39;s">Sainsbury's</a> and one Tesco. In 2014 a small <a href="/wiki/Morrisons" title="Morrisons">Morrisons</a> store opened in the town centre located in the building previously occupied by <a href="/wiki/Burger_King" title="Burger King">Burger King</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Shortly after opening the Morrisons closed and the space was taken by a Foot Asylum.  There are also a variety of small specialist and independent shops, many located in the three-storey Victorian shopping arcade, Byram Arcade, situated on Westgate.
</p><p>However over the last decade many shops have closed down causing a general decline of the town centre<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>. Most notability the closure of <a href="/wiki/British_Home_Stores" title="British Home Stores">British Home Stores (BHS)</a> in 2016 left a large shopping unit empty in The Piazza Centre. In 2019 <a href="/wiki/Marks_%26_Spencer" title="Marks &amp; Spencer">Marks &amp; Spencer</a> announced 17 closures within the UK, one of these is the Huddersfield store.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Entertainment">Entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Entertainment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Batley_Theatre" title="Lawrence Batley Theatre">Lawrence Batley Theatre</a>, opened in 1994, in what was once the largest <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Church_of_Great_Britain" title="Methodist Church of Great Britain">Wesleyan Chapel</a> in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> and presents dance, drama, comedy, music and exhibitions and is the base for Full Body &amp; the Voice, a company focusing on the integration of disabled people into mainstream theatre. Kelly Rowlands also holds the 2003 Line Dancing championship Record.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/John_Smith%27s_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="John Smith&#39;s Stadium">John Smith's Stadium</a>, (formerly the Galpharm Stadium and Alfred McAlpine Stadium), is a multi-use sports stadium with a gym, swimming pool, spa and offers sporting classes. The stadium is home to Huddersfield Giants and Huddersfield Town football team. Adjacent the stadium is an <a href="/wiki/Odeon_Cinemas" title="Odeon Cinemas">Odeon cinema</a> (formerly UCI).
</p><p>There are many pubs, restaurants and night clubs, one of which, <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Industries" title="Tokyo Industries">Tokyo</a>, which closed in 2019, occupies the former Huddersfield <a href="/wiki/County_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="County Court">County Court</a>, a 19th-century <a href="/wiki/Grade_II_listed_building" class="mw-redirect" title="Grade II listed building">Grade II listed building</a>. The oldest pub is the Parish (formerly the Fleece Inn), the pub has been trading since 1720.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As well as primary and secondary schools, which cover compulsory and <a href="/wiki/Sixth_form" title="Sixth form">sixth form</a> education for the town's population, Huddersfield has two <a href="/wiki/Sixth_form_college" title="Sixth form college">sixth form colleges</a>: <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_New_College" title="Huddersfield New College">Huddersfield New College</a> at <a href="/wiki/Salendine_Nook" title="Salendine Nook">Salendine Nook</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greenhead_College" title="Greenhead College">Greenhead College</a> west of the town centre. <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Grammar_School" title="Huddersfield Grammar School">Huddersfield Grammar School</a> is the only independent school for secondary education up to age 16. The town has a <a href="/wiki/Further_education" title="Further education">further education</a> college, <a href="/wiki/Kirklees_College" title="Kirklees College">Kirklees College</a> formed following the merger of Dewsbury College and Huddersfield Technical College. Its one establishment of higher education is the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Huddersfield" title="University of Huddersfield">University of Huddersfield</a> whose chancellor is <a href="/wiki/Prince_Andrew,_Duke_of_York" title="Prince Andrew, Duke of York">the Duke of York</a>. The actor <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Stewart" title="Patrick Stewart">Patrick Stewart</a> from <a href="/wiki/Mirfield" title="Mirfield">Mirfield</a> is emeritus chancellor.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HuddersfieldRoyalInfirmary.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/HuddersfieldRoyalInfirmary.jpg/220px-HuddersfieldRoyalInfirmary.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="99" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/HuddersfieldRoyalInfirmary.jpg/330px-HuddersfieldRoyalInfirmary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/HuddersfieldRoyalInfirmary.jpg/440px-HuddersfieldRoyalInfirmary.jpg 2x" data-file-width="639" data-file-height="288" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HuddersfieldRoyalInfirmary.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Royal_Infirmary" title="Huddersfield Royal Infirmary">Huddersfield Royal Infirmary</a>.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Royal_Infirmary" title="Huddersfield Royal Infirmary">Huddersfield Royal Infirmary</a> is situated in <a href="/wiki/Lindley,_West_Yorkshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Lindley, West Yorkshire">Lindley</a>. Medical services are split between there and the <a href="/wiki/Calderdale_Royal_Hospital" title="Calderdale Royal Hospital">Calderdale Royal Hospital</a> at <a href="/wiki/Salterhebble" title="Salterhebble">Salterhebble</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_West_Yorkshire" title="Halifax, West Yorkshire">Halifax</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kirkwood_Hospice" title="Kirkwood Hospice">Kirkwood Hospice</a> provides care for the <a href="/wiki/Terminal_illness" title="Terminal illness">terminally ill</a>, and is dependent on donations and charitable gifts. Princess Royal Hospital provided <a href="/wiki/Maternity" class="mw-redirect" title="Maternity">maternity</a> facilities until the risks of not being able to get an ambulance to <a href="/wiki/Emergency_department" title="Emergency department">A&amp;E</a> in the event of complications were judged to outweigh the benefits of specialist service provision. It now functions as a day clinic, <a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">family planning</a> consultation centre and <a href="/wiki/Sexual_health_clinic" title="Sexual health clinic">GUM Clinic</a>. A decision to move most maternity services provided by the Calderdale &amp; Huddersfield NHS Foundation Trust to the Calderdale Royal Hospital ended the provision in 2007, despite strong local opposition. The campaign was led by <a href="/wiki/Save_Huddersfield_NHS" title="Save Huddersfield NHS">Save Huddersfield NHS</a> which elected a councillor, Dr Jackie Grunsell in the Crosland Moor ward.  In January 2016 plans were announced to close the A&amp;E department of Huddersfield Royal Infirmary and have all emergency cases go to Calderdale Royal instead. This sparked uproar in local communities as it would mean journeys from some areas of over 40 minutes to and from the hospital assuming that the main road into Halifax was not congested, as it frequently is.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The former <a href="/wiki/St_Luke%27s_Hospital,_Huddersfield" title="St Luke&#39;s Hospital, Huddersfield">St. Luke's Hospital</a> in <a href="/wiki/Crosland_Moor" title="Crosland Moor">Crosland Moor</a> mostly provided <a href="/wiki/Geriatric" class="mw-redirect" title="Geriatric">geriatric</a> and <a href="/wiki/Psychiatric" class="mw-redirect" title="Psychiatric">psychiatric</a> care. It closed in 2011 and the land was sold to a developer.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_civic_honours_and_freedoms">List of civic honours and freedoms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: List of civic honours and freedoms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Thirty-four people and one military (<a href="/wiki/Infantry" title="Infantry">infantry</a>) regiment have been granted the Freedom of Huddersfield, between 1889 and 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Wright Mellor JP DL – (25 September 1889)</li>
<li>Henry Frederick Beaumont JP DL – (28 August 1894)</li>
<li>Lt Col <a href="/wiki/Albert_Rollit" title="Albert Rollit">Sir Albert Kaye Rollit</a> LLD DLC LittD JP DL – (28 August 1894)</li>
<li>James Nield Sykes JP – (12 March 1895)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Woodhead" title="Joseph Woodhead">Joseph Woodhead</a> JP – (28 October 1898)</li>
<li>Sir <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Crosland" title="Joseph Crosland">Joseph Crosland</a> Knt JP DL – (28 October 1898)</li>
<li>Major Charles Brook – (23 May 1901)</li>
<li>Major Harold Wilson – (23 May 1901)</li>
<li>Sir Thomas Brooke Bart JP DL – (25 July 1906)</li>
<li>Rev Robert Bruce MA DD – (25 July 1906)</li>
<li>William Brooke JP – (15 October 1913)</li>
<li>John Sykes JP – (15 October 1913)</li>
<li>William Henry Jessop JP – (18 September 1918)</li>
<li>Earnest Woodhead MA JP – (18 September 1918)</li>
<li>George Thomson JP – (18 September 1918)</li>
<li>Benjamin Broadbent CBE MA JP – (18 September 1918)</li>
<li>John Arthur Brooke MA JP – (18 September 1918)</li>
<li>James Edward Willans JP – (18 September 1918)</li>
<li>Admiral of the Fleet <a href="/wiki/David_Beatty,_1st_Earl_Beatty" title="David Beatty, 1st Earl Beatty">Earl Beatty</a> GCB OM GCVO DSO – (24 July 1920)</li>
<li>The Rt Hon <a href="/wiki/H._H._Asquith" title="H. H. Asquith">H. H. Asquith</a> Earl of Oxford and Asquith, and Viscount Asquith – (6 November 1925)</li>
<li>Sir William Pick Raynor Knt JP – (17 December 1926)</li>
<li>Wilfrid Dawson JP – (25 July 1934)</li>
<li>Rowland Mitchell JP – (25 July 1934)</li>
<li>James Albert Woolven JP Chevalier de la Légion d'honneur – (25 July 1934)</li>
<li>Sir <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Montgomery,_1st_Viscount_Montgomery_of_Alamein" class="mw-redirect" title="Bernard Montgomery, 1st Viscount Montgomery of Alamein">Bernard Law Montgomery</a> Field-Marshal GCB DSO – (26 October 1945)</li>
<li>Joseph Barlow JP – (23 June 1949)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment" title="Duke of Wellington&#39;s Regiment">Duke of Wellington's Regiment (West Riding)</a> – (2 July 1952)</li>
<li>Sidney Kaye LLB – (19 November 1957)</li>
<li>Alderman Arthur Gardiner OBE JP – (11 October 1960)</li>
<li>Alderman Harry Andrew Bennie Gray CBE JP – (11 October 1960)</li>
<li>Sir <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Sargent" title="Malcolm Sargent">Malcolm Sargent</a> MusD(Dunelm) MusD(Oxon)(Hons) LLD(Liverpool) Hon RAM Hon FRCO FRCM FRSA – (13 October 1961)</li>
<li>The Rt Hon <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a> OBE MP Prime Minister and First Lord of the Treasury – (1 March 1968)</li>
<li>Alderman Douglas Graham CBE – (5 March 1973)</li>
<li>Alderman Reginald Harmley MBE JP – (5 March 1973)</li>
<li>Alderman Clifford Stephenson – (5 March 1973)</li></ul>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Freedom_Scroll_DWR_Huddersfield_(RLH).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Freedom_Scroll_DWR_Huddersfield_%28RLH%29.JPG/170px-Freedom_Scroll_DWR_Huddersfield_%28RLH%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Freedom_Scroll_DWR_Huddersfield_%28RLH%29.JPG/255px-Freedom_Scroll_DWR_Huddersfield_%28RLH%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Freedom_Scroll_DWR_Huddersfield_%28RLH%29.JPG/340px-Freedom_Scroll_DWR_Huddersfield_%28RLH%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="921" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Freedom_Scroll_DWR_Huddersfield_(RLH).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>DWR Freedom Scroll</div></div></div>
<p>On 2 July 1952, in recognition of historic ties and links with the <a href="/wiki/The_Duke_of_Wellington%27s_Regiment" class="mw-redirect" title="The Duke of Wellington&#39;s Regiment">Duke of Wellington's Regiment (West Riding)</a>, the Huddersfield County Borough had conferred on the regiment the Freedom of the Town. This gave the regiment the right to march through the town with 'flags flying, bands playing and bayonets fixed'. Many of the town and district's male residents had served in the regiment during its long history. This right to march was technically lost when the County Borough itself was merged with Dewsbury to form Kirklees Metropolitan Borough Council though, unofficially, continued as on 25 March 1979, Kirklees Metropolitan Borough Council gave the Freedom of Kirklees to the 3rd battalion of the Yorkshire Volunteers. The 3rd Battalion was the Duke of Wellington's <a href="/wiki/Territorial_Army_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Territorial Army (United Kingdom)">Territorial Army</a> unit.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yorkshire_Regiment,_Freedom_of_Huddersfield(RLH)2008-10-25.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Yorkshire_Regiment%2C_Freedom_of_Huddersfield%28RLH%292008-10-25.JPG/170px-Yorkshire_Regiment%2C_Freedom_of_Huddersfield%28RLH%292008-10-25.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Yorkshire_Regiment%2C_Freedom_of_Huddersfield%28RLH%292008-10-25.JPG/255px-Yorkshire_Regiment%2C_Freedom_of_Huddersfield%28RLH%292008-10-25.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Yorkshire_Regiment%2C_Freedom_of_Huddersfield%28RLH%292008-10-25.JPG/340px-Yorkshire_Regiment%2C_Freedom_of_Huddersfield%28RLH%292008-10-25.JPG 2x" data-file-width="753" data-file-height="533" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Yorkshire_Regiment,_Freedom_of_Huddersfield(RLH)2008-10-25.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Conferring the Freedom of Huddersfield on the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Regiment" title="Yorkshire Regiment">Yorkshire Regiment</a> 25 October 2008</div></div></div>
<p>When the 'Dukes' were amalgamated with the <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales%27s_Own_Regiment_of_Yorkshire" title="Prince of Wales&#39;s Own Regiment of Yorkshire">Prince of Wales's Own Regiment of Yorkshire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/The_Green_Howards" class="mw-redirect" title="The Green Howards">Green Howards</a>' to form the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Regiment" title="Yorkshire Regiment">Yorkshire Regiment</a> on 6 June 2006. The right to march was finally ended as the award did not give the right, for the freedom to march, to be passed on to any heirs or successors. The majority of the Yorkshire Regiment is now composed of soldiers from the north and eastern areas of Yorkshire. The Yorkshire Regiment requested the right to march to be transferred to them. However, the County Borough no longer exists and so there was no authority to do so. The 'Freedom' given by Kirklees to the 3rd battalion of the Yorkshire Volunteers did not permit any transfer to heirs or successors and effectively that freedom also ceased when the battalion was amalgamated into the <a href="/wiki/East_and_West_Riding_Regiment" title="East and West Riding Regiment">East and West Riding Regiment</a>. The East and West Riding Regiment ceased to exist on 6 June 2006, having been merged into the Yorkshire Regiment as its 4th Battalion. Kirklees Metropolitan Borough Council, as successors to the Huddersfield Borough Council, amended the original 'Freedom' and transferred the 'Freedom' to the Yorkshire Regiment, at a Freedom parade on 25 October 2008.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Huddersfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:People_from_Huddersfield" title="Category:People from Huddersfield">Category: People from Huddersfield</a></div>
<p>A number of national and internationally famous people originate from Huddersfield. Actors include Joanna Christie, James Mason, Gorden Kaye and Keith Buckley.
Some people have also become known through their association with Huddersfield, though they were not born there. These include the <a href="/wiki/Mirfield" title="Mirfield">Mirfield</a>-born actor ("life-long" Huddersfield Town F.C. supporter<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_(education)" title="Chancellor (education)">Chancellor</a> of <a href="/wiki/University_of_Huddersfield" title="University of Huddersfield">Huddersfield University</a> from 2004 to 2015<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>), <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Stewart" title="Patrick Stewart">Patrick Stewart</a>; the dancer, entertainer and TV presenter <a href="/wiki/Roy_Castle" title="Roy Castle">Roy Castle</a>, who was born in <a href="/wiki/Scholes,_Holme_Valley" title="Scholes, Holme Valley">Scholes</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/York" title="York">York</a>-born Olympic gold medal-winning swimmer, <a href="/wiki/Anita_Lonsbrough" title="Anita Lonsbrough">Anita Lonsbrough</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Brighouse" title="Brighouse">Brighouse</a> born inventor <a href="/wiki/Wilf_Lunn" title="Wilf Lunn">Wilf Lunn</a>, who was raised in <a href="/wiki/Rastrick" title="Rastrick">Rastrick</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Other famous people whose association with Huddersfield is not as notable or well-known, though they were raised there, include <a href="/wiki/H._H._Asquith" title="H. H. Asquith">H. H. Asquith</a> (born in <a href="/wiki/Morley,_West_Yorkshire" title="Morley, West Yorkshire">Morley</a>), who served as the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_(UK)" title="Liberal Party (UK)">Liberal</a> Prime Minister of the United Kingdom between 1908 and 1916. The actress <a href="/wiki/Lena_Headey" title="Lena Headey">Lena Headey</a>, who was born in <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>, grew up in <a href="/wiki/Shelley,_West_Yorkshire" title="Shelley, West Yorkshire">Shelley</a> from the age of five.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li><a href="/wiki/Nina_Hossain" title="Nina Hossain">Nina Hossain</a>, journalist and <a href="/wiki/ITN" title="ITN">ITN</a> television presenter <div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harold_Wilson_(1967).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Harold_Wilson_%281967%29.jpg/220px-Harold_Wilson_%281967%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Harold_Wilson_%281967%29.jpg/330px-Harold_Wilson_%281967%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Harold_Wilson_%281967%29.jpg/440px-Harold_Wilson_%281967%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2021" data-file-height="2695" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harold_Wilson_(1967).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister of the United Kingdom</a></div></div></div></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Francis_Ernest_Jackson" title="Francis Ernest Jackson">Francis Ernest Jackson</a>, painter, draughtsman, poster designer and lithographer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cameron_Jerome" title="Cameron Jerome">Cameron Jerome</a>, professional footballer for <a href="/wiki/Derby_County_F.C." title="Derby County F.C.">Derby County</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gorden_Kaye" title="Gorden Kaye">Gorden Kaye</a>, BAFTA-nominated comic actor.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Z%C3%B6e_Lucker" title="Zöe Lucker">Zöe Lucker</a>, actress.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/James_Mason" title="James Mason">James Mason</a>, actor who gained international fame in Hollywood.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jermaine_McGillvary" title="Jermaine McGillvary">Jermaine McGillvary</a>, rugby league player for <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Giants" title="Huddersfield Giants">Huddersfield Giants</a> and <a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_league_team" title="England national rugby league team">England</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vivek_Murthy" title="Vivek Murthy">Vivek Murthy</a>. 19th <a href="/wiki/Surgeon_General_of_the_United_States" title="Surgeon General of the United States">Surgeon General of the United States</a>.</li>
<li>Sir <a href="/wiki/Walter_Parratt" title="Walter Parratt">Walter Parratt</a>, composer and organist.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/DJ_Q" title="DJ Q">DJ Q</a>, disk jockey, radio presenter and producer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wilfred_Rhodes" title="Wilfred Rhodes">Wilfred Rhodes</a>, test and first-class cricketer for <a href="/wiki/England_cricket_team" title="England cricket team">England</a> and Yorkshire County Cricket Club.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Brian_Shaw_(dancer)" title="Brian Shaw (dancer)">Brian Shaw</a>, ballet dancer.<sup id="cite_ref-ODD_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODD-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rod_Smallwood" title="Rod Smallwood">Rod Smallwood</a>, music manager.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jon_Stead" title="Jon Stead">Jon Stead</a>, professional footballer.</li>
<li>Sir <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Stewart" title="Patrick Stewart">Patrick Stewart</a>, actor known for <i>Star Trek: The Next Generation</i> and the Shakespearean stage.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tom_Sykes" title="Tom Sykes">Tom Sykes</a>, World Superbike Champion.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/D._R._Thorpe" title="D. R. Thorpe">D. R. Thorpe</a>, political biographer.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sally_Wainwright" title="Sally Wainwright">Sally Wainwright</a>, English television writer, producer, and director.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_Whitaker_(equestrian)" title="John Whitaker (equestrian)">John Whitaker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Equestrianism" title="Equestrianism">equestrian</a> and former Olympian.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jodie_Whittaker" title="Jodie Whittaker">Jodie Whittaker</a>, actress.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a>, Baron Wilson of Rievaulx, Labour politician and twice <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister of the United Kingdom</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Haydn_Wood" title="Haydn Wood">Haydn Wood</a>, composer and violinist.</li></ul>

<li id="cite_note-haddersfield-84"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-haddersfield_84-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">'During the periods 1822–1832 the 33rd Regiment of Foot, recruited from West Yorkshire was stationed in Jamaica. At the end of the tour 142 men chose to remain in Jamaica, having married and raised families, some of which may have originated from Huddersfield, thereby originating the name. Over 560 officers and men died and were buried in Jamaica during this period, from endemic diseases. On 18 June 1853 the regiment formally became known as "The 33rd (or The Duke of Wellington's) Regiment". The regiment's second battalion was again posted to Jamaica (Newcastle Camp) from 18 March 1891 to 10 April 1893. <cite class="citation book">Brereton, JM; Savory, ACS (1993). <i>The History of the Duke of Wellingtons (West Riding) 1702 – 1992</i>. Halifax: The Duke of Wellington's Regiment. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-9521552-0-6" title="Special:BookSources/0-9521552-0-6"><bdi>0-9521552-0-6</bdi></a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+History+of+the+Duke+of+Wellingtons+%28West+Riding%29+1702+%E2%80%93+1992&amp;rft.pub=Halifax%3A+The+Duke+of+Wellington%27s+Regiment&amp;rft.date=1993&amp;rft.isbn=0-9521552-0-6&amp;rft.aulast=Brereton&amp;rft.aufirst=JM&amp;rft.au=Savory%2C+ACS&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHuddersfield" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
